  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_aa4af0c0-3d53-401a-8e3c-ce6e397554a4'
      });

      <div id="description" class="readable stacked" style="right:0">
        
<span id="freeTextContainer13910043571154300222">Sixteen-year-old Bri wants to be one of the greatest rappers of all time. Or at least make it out of her neighborhood one day. As the daughter of an underground rap legend who died before he hit big, Bri’s got big shoes to fill. But now that her mom has unexpectedly lost her job, food banks and shutoff notices are as much a part of Bri’s life as beats and rhymes. With bill</span>
  <span id="freeText13910043571154300222" style="display:none">Sixteen-year-old Bri wants to be one of the greatest rappers of all time. Or at least make it out of her neighborhood one day. As the daughter of an underground rap legend who died before he hit big, Bri’s got big shoes to fill. But now that her mom has unexpectedly lost her job, food banks and shutoff notices are as much a part of Bri’s life as beats and rhymes. With bills piling up and homelessness staring her family down, Bri no longer just wants to make it—she has to make it.<br /><br /><i>On the Come Up</i> is Angie Thomas’s homage to hip-hop, the art that sparked her passion for storytelling and continues to inspire her to this day. It is the story of fighting for your dreams, even as the odds are stacked against you; of the struggle to become who you are and not who everyone expects you to be; and of the desperate realities of poor and working-class black families.</span>
  <a data-text-id="13910043571154300222" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

<div id="review_2539640412" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2539640412" />
    <a title="chai ♡" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/42130592-chai"><img alt="chai ♡" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1603167303p2/42130592.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2539640412?book_show_action=true">Nov 17, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="chai ♡" class="user" itemprop="url" name="chai ♡" href="/user/show/42130592-chai">chai ♡</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="ebook " href="/book/show/35068618-on-the-come-up">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/42130592-chai?shelf=2019-releases">2019-releases</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/42130592-chai?shelf=fiction">fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/42130592-chai?shelf=read-in-2019">read-in-2019</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/42130592-chai?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/42130592-chai?shelf=poc-rep">poc-rep</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/42130592-chai?shelf=lgbtq-rep-side">lgbtq-rep-side</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/42130592-chai?shelf=ya-contemporary">ya-contemporary</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/42130592-chai?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/42130592-chai?shelf=ya-romance">ya-romance</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/42130592-chai?shelf=own-voices">own-voices</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2539640412" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9895807114012736627"><strong>It’s Angie Thomas’ world and she’s just allowing us to live in it.</strong><br/><br/>You know when you finish reading a book and there's a moment that feels so remarkable it carves out a space in time and whirls there while the world rushes on around it? In that gap where your real storyline seems very abstract and you're left with such a warm and happy feeling that you're glowing just by being around the book's energy?<br/><br/>That was me upon finishing this book. I'm still overwhelmed by the zing of feeling in my heart a</span>
  <span id="freeText9895807114012736627" style="display:none"><strong>It’s Angie Thomas’ world and she’s just allowing us to live in it.</strong><br /><br />You know when you finish reading a book and there's a moment that feels so remarkable it carves out a space in time and whirls there while the world rushes on around it? In that gap where your real storyline seems very abstract and you're left with such a warm and happy feeling that you're glowing just by being around the book's energy?<br /><br />That was me upon finishing this book. I'm still overwhelmed by the zing of feeling in my heart and I think reading Angie Thomas' books should be honestly classified as an official human emotion.<br /><br /><strong>
  <u>So, what’s this book about?</u>
</strong><br /><br />16-year-old Brianna “Bri” Jackson has channeled all her yearning into one fervent dream: to reach rap stardom. She believes in it with as much certainty as a heart can hold.<br /><br />Bri’s memory of her late father—a legendary underground rapper who was shot dead by a rival gang when Bri was 12 years old—has always been like shadows flitting at the corner of her eye, but Bri’s dream always brought his ghost to stand beside her. Bri held that hope in a desperate grip as her widowed mother, a drug addict eight years clean, ekes out a living on a church secretary salary, and her older brother drudges in a minimum-wage job after years of toil for his college degree. It’s what sustained Bri through the phases of dark, until the return to light. A career in rap could turn the tide of her family’s life. There would be no more gray sift of days where they had to choose between electricity and gas, no more diligent waiting for the dreary future to trickle forth.<br /><br />Bri is also one of the few black students who attend an arts school. Following an incident where she is violently targeted by a security guard, determination burns out Bri’s gathering hurt and lyrics burns bright as tinder in her mind, illuminating the dark corners. Bri speaks of her growing frustration with being discriminated against for being black, of her incontinent ambition, of her family’s grinding financial situation and how her chest is weary from carrying all this repeated hope and disappointment, and the words expanded until they blotted out all else.<br /><br />Bri's song soon goes viral and it was like flying into a tornado. The public wrings out real meaning from her lyrics and assigns it their own. They brand Bri a dangerous, angry black girl and a “hoodlum”—a word like a wall and Bri runs against it and can go no further. Bri’s disgrace is encouragement, lowering her enough that everyone dares to reach up, including her father’s sleazy old manager who insists Bri caters to the false image they painted of her in order to make more money. “<em>You know what white kids in the suburbs love? Listening to shit that scares their parents</em>,” he tells her. “<em>You scare the hell outta their folks, they’ll flock to you like birds.</em>”<br /><br />But Bri's strength and resolution run deep. The trek is arduous but the world's wonders are unrolled like a rug before her, and the future is hers for the taking.<br /><br /><blockquote>
  <em><strong>Gift.</strong> One word, one syllable. I don’t know if it rhymes with anything because it’s a word I never thought could be used when it comes to me.</em>
</blockquote><br /><br />Don’t let the charming exterior dupe you—<strong>step into this book and it will step into you.</strong><br /><br /><em>On the Come Up</em> is the kind of story that drags you down so deep that you’re underneath thought, engulfed in a place of pure <em>feeling</em>. It’s a powerful tale—by turns tender and attentive, unyielding and sharp. It made me laugh. It made me crushingly sad. It made me feel like something was growing inside me, like the words were sinking into me and expanding in my chest and it all wanted to spill out in waves of music and silver light.<br /><br />Angie Thomas rolls up her sleeves and tackles Bri’s story with heady mirth. <em>On the Come Up</em> glitters with life, and its conversational, yet profound tone is warm and magnetic when it isn't quietly devastating, and raw as a wound.<br /><br />There’s a prodigious sense of hard, spare <em>wanting</em> in this book that fairly leaps off the page. Bri’s passion is a welter of flame. Just as she is unstoppable and relentless for the ones she loves, she embodies that with her love for rap. She spoke her dream and promptly sealed into the world and woe betide anyone who stands in her way. Her lyrics dug at my bones and made chills shiver across my skin. <strong>I absolutely loved Bri’s character.</strong> Angie keeps her struggles energized and absorbing that you can almost feel it in your blood as well: that iron weight Bri had borne so long, that certain recklessness of temper, nourished by the rough world in which she found herself, which had burst thrillingly to steely determination. It was equally harrowing and thrilling to know that Bri was standing at the precipice of something new and it felt like a gift and a privilege to embark with her on this sublime campaign of life-perfecting.<br /><br /><blockquote>
  <em>“So, who are you?” </em>
  <br />
  <em>“What?” </em>
  <br />
  <em>“Who are you?” she repeats. “Of the millions and billions of people in the world, you’re the only person who can answer that. Not people online or at your school. I can’t even answer that. I can say who I think you are.” She cups my cheek. “And I think you’re brilliant, talented, courageous, beautiful. You’re my miracle. But you’re the only one who can say who you are with authority. So, who are you?”</em>
</blockquote><br /><br />But even more than that, the novel's strength lies in how it succeeds in being both a delightful romp through teenagedom, packed with charisma, firecracker dialogue and well-crafted characters, while also being a bold and illuminating commentary on racism, prejudice, double standards and homophobia. It’s a difficult feat that marks Angie Thomas as a remarkable author to keep your eyes on. <em>On the Come up</em> is set in the same universe as <em>The Hate U Give</em> and the memory of <em>THUG</em>’s tragic events are emblazoned on this book’s pages. Although Starr’s and Bri’s lives could not be any more disparate, the book highlights how discrimination and racism touches them with the same hand, and how it is a constant feature in the lives of the American black community no matter what their socio-economic standing is. I'm excited to see the conversations this book evokes!<br /><br /><strong>But<em> On the Come Up</em> isn’t all grim.</strong> The novel loosens the chokehold of anger and frustration on the reader’s soul by making space for moments of comfort and vicarious happiness. It’s imbued with hope like a small, mad flame flaring in a dark place as the characters learn to lift their arms to hold up their world. I loved Bri’s friendship with Sonny and Malik, and how, despite the occasional quarrel and misunderstanding, they were always supportive of each other. The current of love and hurt and dwindling resentments flowing between Bri and her family also struck me with a deep poignancy.<br /><br />But what sang to me the most is the message that’s wedged deep inside the novel’s heart: <strong>Your voice matters.</strong> You don’t have to bend in order to fit the world’s mold. You don’t have to omit pieces of yourself to ensure someone else’s comfort. You don’t have to stifle your opinion. You don’t have to back-pedal and soften it up to cater to someone else’s measure. Be wonderfully passionate about what’s right. You will draw hatred and animosity no matter what you do, so you might as well make a stand and make it count for something.<br /><br /><blockquote>
  <em>You’ll never silence me and you’ll never kill my dream, Just recognize when you say brilliant that you’re also saying Bri.</em>
</blockquote><br /><br /><em>On the Come Up</em> is equal parts heartrending, insightful, and charming, and as long as Angie Thomas continues to work her marvelous magic, she’ll always have a reader in me!<br /><br /><blockquote>☆ <a href="https://ko-fi.com/givemeabrekk" rel="nofollow noopener">ko-fi</a> ★ <a href="https://bookswithchaima.wordpress.com" rel="nofollow noopener">blog</a> ☆ <a href="https://twitter.com/givemeabrekk" rel="nofollow noopener">twitter</a> ★ <a href="https://azqaban.tumblr.com" rel="nofollow noopener">tumblr</a> ☆</blockquote></span>
  <a data-text-id="9895807114012736627" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

<div id="review_2317443675" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2317443675" />
    <a title="Emily May" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4622890-emily-may"><img alt="Emily May" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1528390751p2/4622890.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2317443675?book_show_action=true">Feb 12, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Emily May" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Emily May" href="/user/show/4622890-emily-may">Emily May</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4622890-emily-may?shelf=contemporary">contemporary</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4622890-emily-may?shelf=botm">botm</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4622890-emily-may?shelf=2019">2019</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4622890-emily-may?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2317443675" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7817650986720316105"><blockquote>
  <i>Aunt Pooh said I only get one chance to let everybody and their momma know who I am. <br/>So I take it.</i>
</blockquote><br/>How do you follow a book like <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/32613366.The_Hate_U_Give' title='The Hate U Give by Angie Thomas' rel='nofollow noopener'>The Hate U Give</a>? <br/><br/>Reading THUG, I got the impression that I was experiencing something momentous. It was breathtaking. Important. I was witnessing a person using their art to say loud and clear “ENOUGH.” <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/35068618.On_the_Come_Up' title='On the Come Up by Angie Thomas' rel='nofollow noopener'>On the Come Up</a> looks at some of the same things, but it is a different kind of book. I think, however, it is a book which shows that Thomas is a great writer, not ju</span>
  <span id="freeText7817650986720316105" style="display:none"><blockquote>
  <i>Aunt Pooh said I only get one chance to let everybody and their momma know who I am. <br />So I take it.</i>
</blockquote><br />How do you follow a book like <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/32613366.The_Hate_U_Give" title="The Hate U Give by Angie Thomas" rel="nofollow noopener">The Hate U Give</a>? <br /><br />Reading THUG, I got the impression that I was experiencing something momentous. It was breathtaking. Important. I was witnessing a person using their art to say loud and clear “ENOUGH.” <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/35068618.On_the_Come_Up" title="On the Come Up by Angie Thomas" rel="nofollow noopener">On the Come Up</a> looks at some of the same things, but it is a different kind of book. I think, however, it is a book which shows that Thomas is a great writer, not just someone who can ride the wave of an important issue.<br /><br />Overall, people will probably like this book less than the author's debut. I've already seen some (understandable) comments about how Bri was a tough character to like compared with Starr. And it's true. Starr is a much easier character to like. She's a clear victim of a screwed-up system; clearly in the right for the whole book. She has very basic easy-to-relate-to relationships with her parents and friends and we are never asked to sympathize with hard-to-like characters. Bri is much more complex.<br /><br />For me, though, <b>she was a far more interesting character than Starr</b>. Her story may not make quite the same impact - being largely about hip hop rather than police shootings - but she herself felt like such an authentic teen voice. She's angry, resentful, impulsive, and outright rude at times. She gets into fights and doesn't play nice. She has a difficult relationship with pretty much everyone in the book. She pushes her family and supporters away, but believes she is doing it to get “on the come up” for them. She considers giving up important parts of herself for a shot at fame and fortune.<br /><br />I can see why some people won't like her, but I actually kinda loved her.<br /><br />I felt every bit of her pain and anger as she watches her family scrape together to try to pay the bills, watches her aunt buried deep in the world of drug dealing, watches security at her school targeting black and Latinx students for searches, watches male rappers make sexist jokes or erase her name and voice because she is a girl. And I loved how she turns to hip hop to make sense of her feelings, finding rhymes in her everyday life and spinning clever verses in her head.<br /><br />As someone who finds books about music a bit hit and miss, I have to say this one was a definite hit. I would have welcomed even more rap. You can tell the author used to be a rapper because Bri's songs are genuinely very good. <a href="https://www.instagram.com/p/BttSj5PHxuH/" rel="nofollow noopener">I'd love to hear them recorded</a>. I also love how she addresses sexism and double standards in the hip hop industry, and points out the ludicrous hypocrisy of a white journalist, who is against gun controls, fearing for her children because of the guns mentioned in rap lyrics. <br /><br />I think this is a great contemporary. A mix of music, family dynamics, fun dialogue, social media and activism, with a protagonist who is moody and difficult and everything I love to read about. I can't wait to see what Thomas writes next.<br /><br /><a href="http://emilymay.me" rel="nofollow noopener">Blog</a> | <a href="https://www.facebook.com/thebookgeekreviews" rel="nofollow noopener">Facebook</a> | <a href="https://twitter.com/thebookgeek01" rel="nofollow noopener">Twitter</a> | <a href="http://instagram.com/emleemay" rel="nofollow noopener">Instagram</a> | <a href="https://www.youtube.com/c/EmilyMayTheBookGeek" rel="nofollow noopener">Youtube</a></span>
  <a data-text-id="7817650986720316105" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

<div id="review_2128535193" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2128535193" />
    <a title="Kai" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/41788524-kai"><img alt="Kai" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1573562141p2/41788524.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2128535193?book_show_action=true">Sep 19, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Kai" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Kai" href="/user/show/41788524-kai">Kai</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9781406372168" href="/book/show/38116316-on-the-come-up">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/41788524-kai?shelf=owned">owned</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/41788524-kai?shelf=2018">2018</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/41788524-kai?shelf=important">important</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/41788524-kai?shelf=feminist-as-fuck">feminist-as-fuck</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2128535193" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12686718828132335362"><i>"You'll never silence me and you'll never kill my dream,<br/>Just recognize when you say brilliant that you're also saying Bri."</i><br/><br/>First of all, HAPPY BOOK BIRTHDAY and second of all THIS BOOK IS GONNA BE A FILM YOU GUYS. What a birthday present, am I right?<br/><br/>Spoiler free!<br/><br/>This is the 2019 release I was most scared to read. THUG was such a major, ground-breaking, and emotional book for me that the stakes for Angie’s second books were mile-high. Now I can assure you that there is no need to worry. Angie wil</span>
  <span id="freeText12686718828132335362" style="display:none"><i>"You'll never silence me and you'll never kill my dream,<br />Just recognize when you say brilliant that you're also saying Bri."</i><br /><br />First of all, HAPPY BOOK BIRTHDAY and second of all THIS BOOK IS GONNA BE A FILM YOU GUYS. What a birthday present, am I right?<br /><br />Spoiler free!<br /><br />This is the 2019 release I was most scared to read. THUG was such a major, ground-breaking, and emotional book for me that the stakes for Angie’s second books were mile-high. Now I can assure you that there is no need to worry. Angie will not disappoint. This book is just as essential and spectacular.<br /><br />I don’t think I have ever read a book this black. I can’t think of a single white main or side character just now. And I know this is going to bother people. Just like they are bothered when there is more than one gay character on a show. White people have been the centre of YA (and the majority of other literary genres) for decades. It is time that popular culture makes room for books that represent and celebrate all kinds of cultures as a whole. This will not only help all kinds of teenagers feel represented, but it will also help us understand each other, it will create empathy, respect, and appreciation. I’m not black, I didn’t grow up in a poor part of town where drugs and gangs shaped society, I have never been discriminated against because my heritage or skin colour led others to think less of me. But this book brought me closer to not only understand the struggles of what a life like Bri’s includes, but also how important loyalty, family, friendship, faith, etc. are for a teenager like her.<br /><br />That’s not all, though. Angie addresses a lot of topics that deal with respecting other people’s backgrounds and stories. She does not pretend to know what is going on in a gay teenagers head but she still manages to tell his story with dignity and tact. She outright acknowledges that a gay boy’s story is not hers to tell because she has not made the same experiences as a presumably straight woman. I would love to see more of that in the literature community overall, not just in YA.<br /><br />Let’s talk about Bri while we’re at it. That girl is talented, lemme tell you. I love her family and friends but I often had a hard time connecting with Bri on an emotional level. She likes to jump to conclusions and often acts without thinking about the consequences. Even when people tell her to watch out and lay low because whatever she might say or do will put her in a difficult position, she still doesn’t stop to think. She keeps making that mistake over and over again and I quickly ran out of patience. Then again, she was hilarious and smart and often made me laugh out loud.<br /><br />The writing was great as always. Reading Angie’s books makes you <i>feel</i> things. The lyrics to Bri’s songs gave me goosebumps every single time. The dialogues between the characters were ultimately funny. So. Much. Shade.<br />There are also a few Easter eggs in there. I am sure that I missed some of them and all I am going to say is that I love seeing authors referencing other authors and their books. Or to see them being inspired by other author’s stories.<br /><br />The reason I’m “only” giving this book 4 stars instead of 5 is because of, as I have mentioned before, the lack of a deeper emotional connection. I seriously wept while reading THUG. That book destroyed me. <i>On the Come Up</i> did not have that effect on me. But as I said, do not let this keep you from reading the book. It is just as compelling as Angie’s debut.<br />I wonder whether we will get to see <i>On the Come Up</i> on the big screen. I would love to actually hear Bri perform her songs. They might become actual chart-toppers, who knows.<br /><br /><i>Thank you to Walker Books for providing me with an advance copy in return for an honest review.</i><br /><br /><a href="https://www.instagram.com/fantasticbooksandwheretofindem/" rel="nofollow noopener">Find more of my books on Instagram</a></span>
  <a data-text-id="12686718828132335362" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2679049207" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2679049207" />
    <a title="megs_bookrack" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/48328025-megs-bookrack"><img alt="megs_bookrack" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1532027727p2/48328025.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2679049207?book_show_action=true">Jan 31, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="megs_bookrack" class="user" itemprop="url" name="megs_bookrack" href="/user/show/48328025-megs-bookrack">megs_bookrack</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2679049207" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4161747824213830312"><b>ANGIE THOMAS!!!</b><br/><br/><img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1453912216ra/17890294.gif' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/>I am <u>so in love</u> with your words.<br/><br/><img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1555697210ra/27386059.gif' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/>This story follows, Bri Jackson, who, like Starr from <i>The Hate U Give</i>, lives in the neighborhood of Garden Heights. <br/><br/>That is pretty much where the similarities end between these two girls.<br/><br/><img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1522664498ra/25310711.gif' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/>Bri lives with her mother and her older brother. Her father, a once successful rapper, was gunned down in the streets, a victim of gang violence. <br/><br/>Bri's mother, a recovering addict, with over 5-years sobriety, is doing her best to provide for her children alone, but </span>
  <span id="freeText4161747824213830312" style="display:none"><b>ANGIE THOMAS!!!</b><br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1453912216ra/17890294.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>I am <u>so in love</u> with your words.<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1555697210ra/27386059.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>This story follows, Bri Jackson, who, like Starr from <i>The Hate U Give</i>, lives in the neighborhood of Garden Heights. <br><br>That is pretty much where the similarities end between these two girls.<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1522664498ra/25310711.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Bri lives with her mother and her older brother. Her father, a once successful rapper, was gunned down in the streets, a victim of gang violence. <br><br>Bri's mother, a recovering addict, with over 5-years sobriety, is doing her best to provide for her children alone, but it's tough.<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1581516015ra/28951952.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Bri has plans to follow in her father's footsteps and she wants to do it her own way. No matter how hard she strives, however, she struggles to find her identity apart from him. <br><br>She is super talented and spends most of her time thinking up rhymes and putting together lyrics. <br><br>She is singularly focused on finding success in order to better the living conditions of herself and her family. To make them 'good'.<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1559230634ra/27593373.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Bri is a great kid, although she has a short fuse. She puts a lot of pressure on herself and I enjoyed getting some insight into her thought process and how she sees the world around her. <br><br>There is always something that seems to be going wrong in her world. It's tough. <br><br>Troubles at school, troubles with bills, being behind in rent and she feels compelled to do something to make it different.<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1581516015ra/28951953.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>I loved this story. The incorporation of Bri's lyrics gave the story such depth. <br><br>I loved that angle, seeing her try to make it and channel her talents for good. Learning to stand her ground and be true to herself. <br><br>I love stories with music, or musicians, as well and this one utilized that trope beautifully.<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1581516015ra/28951954.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>I have read some reviews where readers commented on not enjoying this story as much as <i>THUG</i>. <br><br>That doesn't surprise me, but for me, I sort of feel the opposite. I think I actually enjoyed this one more. While Bri, as a character, may seem contentious, to me, she was perfect.<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1559231001ra/27593392.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>As a 16-year old, many aspects of your life can be extremely frustrating. You can feel like you aren't being heard, like your desires are pushed aside or seen as not important, and that may cause you to act out in socially unacceptable ways. <br><br>I get that. Bri was struggling with some heavy shit and she let it get the best of her sometimes but that happens when you are a kid.<br><br>I liked how this book focused on a variety of hard-hitting issues that can often be brushed over or ignored. <br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1581516015ra/28951955.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>The reality of living in poverty is something that millions of Americans, and people around the world, deal with on a daily basis, and while it isn't pretty, it is important to shine light on and discuss.<br><br>Examples: the fact that Bri's mom was a recovering addict. The fact of the limits that places on her options to provide for her family. <br><br>The way Bri, and other black and brown kids, were treated at her school. The lifestyle Bri's aunt lives and how that affects her entire family. Bri's brother's options for a job after college. <br><br>All of these are difficult issues. I appreciated how much substance Thomas put into this. This was far from a one issue story. <br><br>This was the whole cake and I was eating every bite!<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1581516015ra/28951956.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>I can see why this format may not sit well with everyone. It punches the whole way through, but it is an exceptionally told story. <br><br>Thomas is a true wordsmith. Her writing leaps off the page with realness...is that a word? Realness? <br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1453382302ra/17819504.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>You know what I'm saying. <br><br>As you can tell, I loved this. I want everyone to read it and seriously, I am on the EDGE of my seat until Angie Thomas puts out another book. <br><br>I am really hoping for another story set in Garden Heights!!!</span>
  <a data-text-id="4161747824213830312" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2247631772?book_show_action=true">Feb 12, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Chelsea (chelseadolling reads)" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Chelsea (chelseadolling reads)" href="/user/show/16219087-chelsea-chelseadolling-reads">Chelsea (chelseadolling reads)</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2247631772" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2631213376646322685">While I didn't enjoy the plot of this one quite as much as I enjoyed the plot of the Hate U Give, this book was still soOoOoOoOo GOOD. Angie Thomas' writing perfectly fits the YA genre and we are truly blessed to be living in the same lifetime as her. SO DAMN GOOD.<br/><br/>TW: racism, drug dealing, gun violence</span>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2716331787" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2716331787" />
    <a title="Hannah Greendale" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/43377498-hannah-greendale"><img alt="Hannah Greendale" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1466436186p2/43377498.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2716331787?book_show_action=true">Feb 15, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Hannah Greendale" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Hannah Greendale" href="/user/show/43377498-hannah-greendale">Hannah Greendale</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/43377498-hannah-greendale?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/43377498-hannah-greendale?shelf=contemporary">contemporary</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2716331787" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13782464754720850170">Going to keep this review short because everyone and their rap-loving aunt is going to read and review this book. And, cutting right to the chase, because everyone wants to know how <i>On the Come Up</i> measures up to <i>The Hate U Give</i>, so let me be straight: They're <i>different</i> books. <br/><br/>THUG is about a girl, a victim, being shuffled along by something much bigger than her - a socio-political movement hundreds of years in the making. Starr Carter is a quiet girl, a good girl, who tries to keep to herself an</span>
  <span id="freeText13782464754720850170" style="display:none">Going to keep this review short because everyone and their rap-loving aunt is going to read and review this book. And, cutting right to the chase, because everyone wants to know how <i>On the Come Up</i> measures up to <i>The Hate U Give</i>, so let me be straight: They're <i>different</i> books. <br /><br />THUG is about a girl, a victim, being shuffled along by something much bigger than her - a socio-political movement hundreds of years in the making. Starr Carter is a quiet girl, a good girl, who tries to keep to herself and waits until pretty late in the game to find her voice. <br /><br />That's not Bri. She's anything but quiet. This is <i>her</i> story. Action is driven, not by exterior forces, but by the choices <i>she</i> makes. <i>On the Come Up</i> is an intimate, interpersonal, tight narrative focused on one girl and the consequences of her actions in pursuit of her dream. Bri is flawed, driven, relatable. Her story is inner-city life, hip-hop, self-discovery and self-image rolled into one. <br /><br />THUG is about <i>external</i> conflict. OTCU is about <i>internal</i> conflict. They're <i>different</i> books, but they're both written by a gifted author who boldly explores themes of systemic racism, racial inequality, social injustice, and gang violence and who excels at crafting authentic voice and believable characters. <br /><blockquote>
  <i>Milez glares at me as he raps. Something about how much money he has, how many girls like him, his clothes, his jewelry, the ganster life he's living. Repetitive. Stale. Prewritten. <br /><br />I gotta go for the kill. <br /><br />Here I am, going at him as if I don't have any manners. Manners. A lot of words rhyme with that if I deliver them right. Cameras. Rappers. Pamper. Hammer - MC Hammer. Vanilla Ice. Hip-hop heads consider them pop stars, not real rappers. I can compare him to them. <br /><br />I gotta get my signature line in there - you can only spell "brilliant" with Bri. Aunt Pooh once pointed that out right before teasing me about being such a perfectionist. [. . .]<br /><br />Milez lowers the mic. There are a couple of cheers. Supreme claps, yet his face is hard. <br /><br />"Okay, I see you, Milez!" Hype says. "Bri, you better bring the heat!" <br /><br />The instrumental starts up again. Aunt Pooh said I only get one chance to let everybody and their momma know who I am. <br /><br />So I take it.</i>
</blockquote></span>
  <a data-text-id="13782464754720850170" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2681513406" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2681513406" />
    <a title="Lilith Black Bee" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/8095953-lilith-black-bee"><img alt="Lilith Black Bee" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1563487061p2/8095953.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2681513406?book_show_action=true">Feb 10, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Lilith Black Bee" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Lilith Black Bee" href="/user/show/8095953-lilith-black-bee">Lilith Black Bee</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="ebook " href="/book/show/35068618-on-the-come-up">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2681513406" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5241584031849644513"><b><u>DISCLAIMER</u><br/>I get that some people might not see some of my words with good eyes, but these are the things that this book made me think about. So please, respect my opinion. It's against no one, but if you have a different opinion than mine, or you totally disagree with my thoughts, feel free to say your opinion. I will respect it, no matter what.</b><br/><p>When I found out about this book, I think it was a couple of months ago or something like that. Obviously, I wanted to read this one too after I loved "T</p></span>
  <span id="freeText5241584031849644513" style="display:none"><b><u>DISCLAIMER</u><br />I get that some people might not see some of my words with good eyes, but these are the things that this book made me think about. So please, respect my opinion. It's against no one, but if you have a different opinion than mine, or you totally disagree with my thoughts, feel free to say your opinion. I will respect it, no matter what.</b><br /><p>When I found out about this book, I think it was a couple of months ago or something like that. Obviously, I wanted to read this one too after I loved "The Hate U Give". I was wondering what new story Angie will give us this time. I didn't want to know anything about this book, so I just got blind on it, knowing that the chance to not like it was almost inexistent.</p><br /><p>The way she puts on the paper problems like racism, drugs, poverty, police brutality against black people, and other things like this, is outstanding. She gets us to understand why black people are doing some things, how they think, why they react in the way they do it to the most atrocities against them. In this masterpiece, she shows us that black people have feelings too, even if they are drug dealers, rap artists or gang members. They are humans with feelings, with dreams, with expectations, just like the rest of us. True, they may have more "balls" than the rest of us, sometimes, but this doesn't mean they have to be put in the corner just because their skin color is not white.</p><p></p><br /><p>This is a brilliant insight into their lives, their minds, and their hearts. They can cry and love and hope, just like the rest of us. And you know what? We also can be drug dealers, gang members and what other bad things we put them on the corner for, just like them. Sometimes even with more "talent" than them. But you know what we can't really do like them? We can't really stick to our family like them. Because black people, no matter what, they stick and support their families, exactly how Angie shows us in her book. We can say about us, white people, the same thing? Yes, there are white people like this too, a lot of them, but the big majority can easily leave their family behind for various reasons. And about this, we, white people that can so easily judge black ones, and put them in the corner even for the thing that they speak their mind, I think we have some things to learn from them.</p><p></p><br /><p> The only thing that separates us, is just the skin color. This is all! And Angie Thomas shows this to us in one of the most beautiful and brilliant ways. I am waiting for her next book, the way I am waiting to have my next breath when I am underwater.</p><p></p></span>
  <a data-text-id="5241584031849644513" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2699863897" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2699863897" />
    <a title="Hamad" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/54464244-hamad"><img alt="Hamad" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1577880699p2/54464244.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2699863897?book_show_action=true">Feb 02, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Hamad" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Hamad" href="/user/show/54464244-hamad">Hamad</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="ebook " href="/book/show/35068618-on-the-come-up">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/54464244-hamad?shelf=e-books">e-books</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/54464244-hamad?shelf=2019-reads">2019-reads</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2699863897" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7212483413356314354"> This review and other non-spoilery reviews can be found <a href='https://thebookprescription.wordpress.com/2019/02/12/on-the-come-up-review/' rel='nofollow noopener'>@The Book Prescription</a><br/><br/> <i>“There’s only so much you can take being described as somebody you’re not.” </i><br/><br/>🌟 If Angie Thomas taught me something is that I should use my voice if I have one and I am going to do exactly that. If you think you will be offended by this review or by this not being my favorite book of the year then don’t continue this review!<br/><br/>🌟 A thing I have noticed lately is that it is always a bit harder to view diverse books. For me </span>
  <span id="freeText7212483413356314354" style="display:none"> This review and other non-spoilery reviews can be found <a href="https://thebookprescription.wordpress.com/2019/02/12/on-the-come-up-review/" rel="nofollow noopener">@The Book Prescription</a><br /><br /> <i>“There’s only so much you can take being described as somebody you’re not.” </i><br /><br />🌟 If Angie Thomas taught me something is that I should use my voice if I have one and I am going to do exactly that. If you think you will be offended by this review or by this not being my favorite book of the year then don’t continue this review!<br /><br />🌟 A thing I have noticed lately is that it is always a bit harder to view diverse books. For me personally I am going to be fair to a book regardless of who wrote it and just because a book is diverse does not make it good.<br /><br />🌟 I loved THUG and I got both an E-book and a hardcover of that book, so you bet I was excited for this. Unfortunately it did not live to the hype for me! I know writing a second book can be harder than the first one specially when it gets the recognition that Angie’s debut got (A 100 weeks as a NYT Bestseller and most as #1, that’s just crazy awesome).<br /><br />🌟 I felt that the writing in this one was mediocre, I did not have that feeling of wanting to read the book non-stop. I am also starting to get annoyed by the HP references in many YA books. I used to enjoy them but now they are kind of a bookish pet peeve for me in writing. I know many authors were affected by that series but I think of them as a shortcut to being relatable which annoys me.<br /><br />🌟 I am not the biggest fan of Hip-Hop so I knew I won’t relate as other readers. That being said I expected it to be more enjoyable. I did not know where the story was going. I felt like it is a milder version of THUG ¯\_(ツ)_/¯ .<br /><br />🌟 I also did not have that connection to the characters as I did in THUG. There was no emotions on my part while reading this. I was annoyed by Bri’s actions. I like when YA characters act their ages and are stupid and do things wrong. But Bri’s insisting on being an outlaw was bothersome.<br /><br />🌟 Summary: I ma have had higher expectation from the book which resulted in my being disappointed. The book was not bad but was no where as good as THUG for me personally. The characters, writing and plot were just too meh for my taste. I can’t believe I am saying this but this is a book that I think will be better as a movie!</span>
  <a data-text-id="7212483413356314354" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2597215638" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2597215638" />
    <a title="Nenia ✨️ Socially Awkward Trash Panda ✨️ Campbell" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2190064-nenia-socially-awkward-trash-panda-campbell"><img alt="Nenia ✨️ Socially Awkward Trash Panda ✨️ Campbell" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1584062476p2/2190064.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2597215638?book_show_action=true">Nov 17, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Nenia ✨️ Socially Awkward Trash Panda ✨️ Campbell" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Nenia ✨️ Socially Awkward Trash Panda ✨️ Campbell" href="/user/show/2190064-nenia-socially-awkward-trash-panda-campbell">Nenia ✨️ Socially Awkward Trash Panda ✨️ Campbell</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="ebook " href="/book/show/35068618-on-the-come-up">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2190064-nenia-socially-awkward-trash-panda-campbell?shelf=why-the-hype">why-the-hype</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2190064-nenia-socially-awkward-trash-panda-campbell?shelf=ya-ya-land">ya-ya-land</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2190064-nenia-socially-awkward-trash-panda-campbell?shelf=poc-interracial">poc-interracial</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2597215638" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15221139912233983664"><a href='http://readasaurus.blogspot.com/' rel='nofollow noopener'>
  <img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1459070464i/18565492.jpg' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/>
</a><br/><a href='https://www.instagram.com/neniagram/' rel='nofollow noopener'>Instagram</a> || <a href='https://twitter.com/NeniaCampbell' rel='nofollow noopener'>Twitter</a> || <a href='https://www.facebook.com/aficionenias/' rel='nofollow noopener'>Facebook</a> || <a href='http://www.amazon.com/Nenia-Campbell/e/B00AWVRKMS' rel='nofollow noopener'>Amazon</a> || <a href='https://www.pinterest.com/mightbeamisprin/' rel='nofollow noopener'>Pinterest</a><br/><br/><br/>So apparently giving supporting details about your arguments = spoilers. I thought I was pretty vague, apart from mentioning a few potentially triggering situations, but just in case: I talk about the book in this review of the book(!), please consider yourself warned. <br/><br/><br/><br/>I've been looking forward to ON THE COME UP ever since I heard that Angie Thomas was writing a new book. <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1972076943' rel='nofollow noopener'>THE HATE U GIVE</a> was one of those life-changing books for me, in th</span>
  <span id="freeText15221139912233983664" style="display:none"><a href="http://readasaurus.blogspot.com/" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1459070464i/18565492.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><a href="https://www.instagram.com/neniagram/" rel="nofollow noopener">Instagram</a> || <a href="https://twitter.com/NeniaCampbell" rel="nofollow noopener">Twitter</a> || <a href="https://www.facebook.com/aficionenias/" rel="nofollow noopener">Facebook</a> || <a href="http://www.amazon.com/Nenia-Campbell/e/B00AWVRKMS" rel="nofollow noopener">Amazon</a> || <a href="https://www.pinterest.com/mightbeamisprin/" rel="nofollow noopener">Pinterest</a><br><br><br>So apparently giving supporting details about your arguments = spoilers. I thought I was pretty vague, apart from mentioning a few potentially triggering situations, but just in case: I talk about the book in this review of the book(!), please consider yourself warned. <br><br><br><br>I've been looking forward to ON THE COME UP ever since I heard that Angie Thomas was writing a new book. <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1972076943" rel="nofollow noopener">THE HATE U GIVE</a> was one of those life-changing books for me, in that it was a pitch-perfect book that came out at a time when the subject material was relevant and necessary, and delivered an emotionally-charged story about institutionalized racism, as well as the importance of movements like <i>Black Lives Matter </i>that shine a much-needed spotlight on racial injustice.<br><br><br><br>ON THE COME UP is a similar story in that it also features a girl in Garden Heights who comes from a low-income family and deals with gang violence and gang activity on a day-to-day basis. Bri's mother is a recovering drug addict and her aunt is in the local gang, the Garden Disciples. Her father was a famous up-and-coming rapper who was murdered. People make assumptions about her just because of the color of her skin and where she comes from, and a racially-targeted bag search that ends in violence inspires Bri to write a rap song that ends up going viral.<br><br><br><br>I really wanted to like this book, but it didn't have the same strength in writing that THE HATE U GIVE had. Starr was a compelling protagonist and it was a really emotional read. ON THE COME UP was emotionally distant, by comparison, and Bri was such an awful heroine. She made one terrible choice after another and treated her friends and family like garbage. I hated the way she talked to her mother, and how she called her mother by her first name with such a lack of respect. I hated the way she treated her friend, and how she made a move on her <i>taken </i>friend who was in a relationship. She also wrote a song with very vivid references to gang activity, which is fine, but then she tried to deny that that wasn't what the song was about when she was called on it. Um, what?<br><br><br><br>Here's the thing, ON THE COME UP was trying to tackle some weighty issues just like THE HATE U GIVE did. This book was about the hypocrisy of white people when it comes to guns (OK when white people have them, thuggish and scary when black people have them), cultural appropriation (white people listening to and consuming rap but not wanting to think about the deeper issues and sociocultural suffering and struggles endemic to the black community due to oppression and injustice), and, of course, institutionalized racism leading to the disenfranchisement, abuse, and even murders of black people over infractions that white people would get minor consequences for.<br><br><br><br>The issue with Bri and her school was not resolved in a satisfactory way. They gave her mother a job, sure, but that felt more like they were trying to buy the family's silence and not a moral turnaround. Bri didn't really advance as a character. She ran around doing and saying whatever she wanted and didn't want to take ownership for her actions or the consequences of her actions. At the end of the book, she's basically rewarded for acting like a total shit because of her raps, and the other problematic aspects of her behavior - getting involved in gang wars, siccing her <i>aunt </i>on a rival gang member despite knowing it could end up in murder, failing in school and treating her tests like they're unimportant, ghosting her friends and/or snapping in their faces, and bitching at her mom - are all basically ignored, because oh,<i> </i>she belatedly became part of a movement and then capitalized on it for financial gain and fame, isn't she a good person? Lmao, her friends basically did all the work getting that movement started, and in the beginning she treated them like trash for it. What in the ever-loving heck? Am I supposed to root for this girl? I mean, I get the fear of wanting to get involved against the same authority figures that oppress you and mistreat you, but letting her friends take the fall for her and then jumping on their shit was totally disgusting and I hated her for it. The writing in this book was a real step-down from THE HATE U GIVE, and seemed unpolished and clunky in comparison. Starr was such a great character, and I loved her so much. Bri was a brat, and the best moment in this book was when her mother gives her a real dressing down over her behavior. #TeamJay<br><br><br><br>Honestly, Jay(da) was the star of this book. I loved Bri's mom. She had <i>so much </i>to deal with, and some of her quotes in this book about racism and police brutality and inequality really reminded me of Starr. I almost wish that this was an adult book about parenting and that Jay(da) had been the heroine, because I was much more interested in hearing about her story than Bri's. Yes, the raps were great and had good flow, and I enjoyed them, but I hated that Bri wrote them because I hated Bri. Jay had to deal with lingering biases over her drug use (including her own daughter), despite being eight years sober. She's in college trying to better her education so she can get a good job, while taking care of two kids and dealing with her deceased husband's younger sister, who's a leader in a gang. The most emotional parts in this book all involved her, especially when she goes to Bri's school to speak up about the racist treatment of her ungrateful shit of a daughter. That packed a punch.<br><br><br><br>Huge disappointment. I was wondering why more of my friends hadn't reviewed this book already and I'm guessing maybe they either didn't like it and didn't want to say so, or they were leery about reading the follow-up book from a successful debut author without reading advance reviews. Well, I didn't like this book and I'm flummoxed at the people saying that this was better than THUG. It really wasn't. If anything, this reads like a debut novel, because of how unsteady it is on its own two legs.<br><br><br><br>I'm so bummed that I can't say great things about ON THE COME UP. :/<br><br><br><br>2 stars</span>
  <a data-text-id="15221139912233983664" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2296776438" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2296776438" />
    <a title="✨    jamieson   ✨" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/7706640-jamieson"><img alt="✨    jamieson   ✨" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1499961431p2/7706640.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2296776438?book_show_action=true">Feb 15, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="✨    jamieson   ✨" class="user" itemprop="url" name="✨    jamieson   ✨" href="/user/show/7706640-jamieson">✨    jamieson   ✨</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9781406372168" href="/book/show/38116316-on-the-come-up">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7706640-jamieson?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7706640-jamieson?shelf=contemporary">contemporary</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7706640-jamieson?shelf=2019-reads">2019-reads</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7706640-jamieson?shelf=audiobook">audiobook</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7706640-jamieson?shelf=favourite-covers">favourite-covers</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7706640-jamieson?shelf=owned-books">owned-books</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2296776438" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17845243667690248958"><i>
  <blockquote>“You’ll never silence me and you’ll never kill my dream. Just recognize when you say brilliant that you’re also saying Bri.”</blockquote>
</i><br/><br/>OH, this was absolutely 100% amazing and Angie Talent is WAY too talented for me to handle. Obviously, I literally adored <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1890354486?book_show_action=false&from_review_page=1>The%20Hate%20U%20Give</a>%20and%20it%20was%20one%20of%20my%20favourite%20reads%20of%20last%20year.%20I%20definitely%20felt%20like%20Angie%20Thomas%20had%20a%20lot%20to%20top,%20and%20I%20think%20that%20worry%20about%20not%20loving%20this%20as%20much%20as%20The%20Hate%20U%20Give%20is%20why%20I%20put%20it%20off%20for%20so%20long.%20But%20I%20did%20Not%20need%20to%20put%20this%20off%20-%20in%20On%20The%20Come%20Up%20Angie%20Thomas%20writes%20with%20the%20same%20brilliance%20and%20authenticity%20that%20made%20me%20fall%20in%20love%20with%20her%20in%20the%20same%20place.%20<br%20/><br%20/>On%20the%20Come%20Up%20follows%20Bri,%20a%20sixteen-year-old%20who%20wants%20to%20be%20a%20rapper%20like%20her%20dad.%20It%27s%20always%20been%20her%20dream,%20but%20she%20also%20thinks%20a%20rap%20career%20could%20be%20her%20and%20her%20families%20ticket%20out%20of%20the%20Garden,%20and%20into%20a%20better%20financial%20situation.%20<br%20/><br%20/>After%20a%20lucky%20break,%20Bri%20gets%20the%20opportunity%20to%20record%20her%20debut%20song%20' rel='nofollow noopener'></a><br/><i>
  <blockquote>“There's only so much you can take being described as somebody you're not.” </blockquote>
</i><br/><br/><b>Easily my favourite part of this book was Bri's character.</b> Bri is the kind of character I've been wanting and needing in YA for so long. She feels so genuinely teen and s</span>
  <span id="freeText17845243667690248958" style="display:none"><i>
  <blockquote>“You’ll never silence me and you’ll never kill my dream. Just recognize when you say brilliant that you’re also saying Bri.”</blockquote>
</i><br /><br />OH, this was absolutely 100% amazing and Angie Talent is WAY too talented for me to handle. Obviously, I literally adored <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1890354486?book_show_action=false&amp;from_review_page=1&gt;The%20Hate%20U%20Give&lt;/a&gt;%20and%20it%20was%20one%20of%20my%20favourite%20reads%20of%20last%20year.%20I%20definitely%20felt%20like%20Angie%20Thomas%20had%20a%20lot%20to%20top,%20and%20I%20think%20that%20worry%20about%20not%20loving%20this%20as%20much%20as%20The%20Hate%20U%20Give%20is%20why%20I%20put%20it%20off%20for%20so%20long.%20But%20I%20did%20Not%20need%20to%20put%20this%20off%20-%20in%20On%20The%20Come%20Up%20Angie%20Thomas%20writes%20with%20the%20same%20brilliance%20and%20authenticity%20that%20made%20me%20fall%20in%20love%20with%20her%20in%20the%20same%20place.%20&lt;br%20/&gt;&lt;br%20/&gt;On%20the%20Come%20Up%20follows%20Bri,%20a%20sixteen-year-old%20who%20wants%20to%20be%20a%20rapper%20like%20her%20dad.%20It%27s%20always%20been%20her%20dream,%20but%20she%20also%20thinks%20a%20rap%20career%20could%20be%20her%20and%20her%20families%20ticket%20out%20of%20the%20Garden,%20and%20into%20a%20better%20financial%20situation.%20&lt;br%20/&gt;&lt;br%20/&gt;After%20a%20lucky%20break,%20Bri%20gets%20the%20opportunity%20to%20record%20her%20debut%20song%20" rel="nofollow noopener"></a><br /><i>
  <blockquote>“There's only so much you can take being described as somebody you're not.” </blockquote>
</i><br /><br /><b>Easily my favourite part of this book was Bri's character.</b> Bri is the kind of character I've been wanting and needing in YA for so long. She feels so genuinely teen and she makes a lot of mistakes that stem from inexperience and her young age but that is what I loved about it. Bri can be brash, harsh, rude, and act without thinking (so many times) but I felt a bit of myself in her recklessness and identified with her teenage angst. I really love that Angie Thomas decided to write a character that really fucks up, and that is really outspoken, it's refreshing. But it's not just her flaws that made me love her - Bri has so many strengths too! she has a heart of gold, is trying to do her best, and loves her friends and family with so much of her heart. She's ambitious and cool, and funny - and damn, I loved the hell outta that girl! <br /><br />Plot wise, this was a lot more fun than The Hate U Give. It still has a lot of the hallmarks of that book though. It deals with racism and growing up as a black teenager in America. It has strong family dynamics, and friendship focus. The focus on family, especially, was a highlight. Angie Thomas knows how to drill down into the core of a family and examine what makes each one tick, and I love the portrayal of the family in this book. <br /><br />This book also just had so much love and heart in it - you could tell. You could tell Thomas loves rap music and hip-hop, she loved her main character, and she loved writing this book. I think that passion and care really leaked onto the pages and it made <b>me care</b>. This book is about music and family but you don't need to care about music to be invested - it just seems to grab you and in a minute you realise you're a hundred pages deep and so invested in the story and the characters. I love that in books. <br /><br /><i>
  <blockquote>“All these folks I've never met became gods over my life. Now I gotta take the power back.”</blockquote>
</i><br /><br />Overall, I think this was just as good as THUG - just in a different way. It's kind of sad to me people seem to have slept on this book a bit because it's great and has so many themes people can connect with. It's a YA book that isn't afraid to shove a loud and bossy main character into the forefront - and to celebrate them for those traits. It's a book that blends rap and friends and family, that has the hallmark YA tropes like first love and family issues, while also exploring race issues in America in a genuine way that only an #ownvoices author can. <br /><br />I also loved the audiobook for this a lot - the narrator sings the raps and its PERFECT. <br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="17845243667690248958" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2207859924" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2207859924" />
    <a title="C.G. Drews" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/11375137-c-g-drews"><img alt="C.G. Drews" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1521552918p2/11375137.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2207859924?book_show_action=true">Feb 19, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="C.G. Drews" class="user" itemprop="url" name="C.G. Drews" href="/user/show/11375137-c-g-drews">C.G. Drews</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9781406372168" href="/book/show/38116316-on-the-come-up">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/11375137-c-g-drews?shelf=read-2019">read-2019</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/11375137-c-g-drews?shelf=contemporary">contemporary</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/11375137-c-g-drews?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2207859924" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2587298721637485750"><b>Well we all knew the Queen of YA would gift us with another incredible story</b>...so brb, just feeling so many things about this one. I also really love Angie Thomas' style, her voice, and her passion and love that you can absolutely feel in every single page of the book. This one is about rapping and being poor and figuring out who you are, no matter what the world is saying or where it's telling you that you fit. It's not quite as dark as <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/32075671.The_Hate_U_Give' title='The Hate U Give by Angie Thomas' rel='nofollow noopener'>The Hate U Give</a>, but that doesn't make it any less powerfu</span>
  <span id="freeText2587298721637485750" style="display:none"><b>Well we all knew the Queen of YA would gift us with another incredible story</b>...so brb, just feeling so many things about this one. I also really love Angie Thomas' style, her voice, and her passion and love that you can absolutely feel in every single page of the book. This one is about rapping and being poor and figuring out who you are, no matter what the world is saying or where it's telling you that you fit. It's not quite as dark as <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/32075671.The_Hate_U_Give" title="The Hate U Give by Angie Thomas" rel="nofollow noopener">The Hate U Give</a>, but that doesn't make it any less powerful or needed! <br /><br />(I maybe liked THUG more, but I also don't want to compare them, because they're different!)<br /><br /><b> ➸ So first things first: rapping.</b><br />Bri's #1 dream is to be a rapper and she's pretty downright good at it. But she writes a song that gets misconstrued and her career sort of snowballs from there. Now, I know zero about rapping ok. So I wont' pretend to have an opinion on this except (1) there are some powerful lyrics going on in this book, (2) I cannot frikkin' wait for the movie version, and (3) I believe Angie Thomas herself is a rapper, so I can imagine a lot of talent and love went into this part of the story! There were a lot of volleying opinions about Bri's rap too: like her family was <i>not</i> happy about her talking about guns and defiance, but Bri was writing about what the world expected her to be anyway.<br /><br />➸<b>Also can we just appreciate Bri for a second???</b><br />She's amazing. She is a geek (and SO TIRED of how most people in her neighbourhood have zero clue what any of her geek culture references are) and she's so protective and loving towards her little messed up family. I mean they're massively struggling. They're super poor (to the point of sometimes there is no food), her mum is struggling to get a job because of her past addictions, Bri's dad got murdered when she was little and she got abandoned by her mum who fell to drugs and took a long time to rebuild. But their family is EPIC and tight and the banter and dialogue is my favourite thing. A+++ to how Angie Thomas always gives us such epic families!! Trey is such a big brother sweetheart with a tough side, and her mum is badass as well as being vulnerable.<br /><br />And Bri has a whip-sharp temper and she's so passionate. I loved this about her. But of course this lands her with the labels of being "that sassy black girl" (which she is <i>furious</i> to be stereotyped) and being aggressive...just for having an opinion. She's definitely not perfect of course. She's 16 and she doesn't know everything and she makes crappy decisions. I really felt for her afjdslkafd. <br /><br />And omg I love her friend squad!! So we have Bri and her two besties, Sonny (who is gay and an artist) and Malik (who loves film and Bri has a Secret Crush on him but that goes...badly lolol). They've been friends since forever, but they're all changing, and I just loved their dynamics. They joke and they fight and I just wanted them to be good !!! friendships get me every time in books. The BEST.<br /><br />➸ <b>Also the romance was so smol but so cute.</b><br />It was definitely a tiny sidedish of the story, but I loved it! And it was a budding romance, so it was cute to see it unfurl amongst the other messes happening for Bri.<br /><br />➸<b> The themes are so so good for this too.</b><br />I mean, but of course. This book has arrived to talk, and it's talking loudly. It unpacks racial profiling and prejudice, it talks about what it really means to be poor, and it talks about defining yourself even though others try to do it for you. There's also a lot of talk about consequences here...ahhh, they often hurt. I'm not American or black, so I definitely want to step back and not pretend to know everything about how Bri felt with living in the hood and struggling with hating stereotypes but wanting to be herself and speak out. I just wanted to quietly read this and absorb it from an #ownvoices author.<br /><br />➸ <b>Also the writing?! YES.</b><br />Dude, I laughed out loud. And I felt all twisted up with anxious nerves. Like, again it wasn't as dark as THUG, so I didn't feel wrecked reading it. But the emotion was palpable. And some of the lines just totally cracked me up. Also it felt like the 450 page book just swished by so fast?! The book is addictive and Bri's voice is so easy to love.<br /><br /><br /><b>Obviously this is one you don't want to miss!!</b> I loved it so much and seriously cannot wait for Thomas' next book announcement. (pls be soon...)</span>
  <a data-text-id="2587298721637485750" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>
