  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2880901354?book_show_action=true">Jul 06, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="BernLuvsBooks " class="user" itemprop="url" name="BernLuvsBooks " href="/user/show/3087404-bernluvsbooks">BernLuvsBooks </a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3087404-bernluvsbooks?shelf=ya-books">ya-books</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3087404-bernluvsbooks?shelf=2019">2019</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3087404-bernluvsbooks?shelf=botm">botm</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2880901354" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1339348698784289732"><b>Angie Thomas has such a way of incorporating social justice (and injustice) into her stories that is both moving and eye opening.</b> This book focused on so many things - racism, drugs, poverty, family issues, being true to yourself and more & it dealt with each one undeniably well. <br/><br/>I was worried going into this book that it wouldn't live up to The Hate You Give for me. While THUG is still my favorite, Bri and her family and friends definitely captured me. I was fully invested in the characters and</span>
  <span id="freeText1339348698784289732" style="display:none"><b>Angie Thomas has such a way of incorporating social justice (and injustice) into her stories that is both moving and eye opening.</b> This book focused on so many things - racism, drugs, poverty, family issues, being true to yourself and more &amp; it dealt with each one undeniably well. <br /><br />I was worried going into this book that it wouldn't live up to The Hate You Give for me. While THUG is still my favorite, Bri and her family and friends definitely captured me. I was fully invested in the characters and their story. Thomas' ability to fully capture the community and people around her main characters is one of the things I love most about her books. <br /><br />One recommendation I would make if this one is on your TBR - consider the audiobook! There are lots of infused rap lyrics and I highly doubt I did all the rap battles justice. It would have been awesome to hear them aloud. I have no doubt it would make for an even more amazing reading experience.</span>
  <a data-text-id="1339348698784289732" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2565618289" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2565618289" />
    <a title="Christy" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/11284813-christy"><img alt="Christy" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1594293998p2/11284813.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2565618289?book_show_action=true">Feb 07, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Christy" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Christy" href="/user/show/11284813-christy">Christy</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="ebook " href="/book/show/35068618-on-the-come-up">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/11284813-christy?shelf=2019-three-stars-and-below">2019-three-stars-and-below</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/11284813-christy?shelf=2019-audio">2019-audio</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/11284813-christy?shelf=2019-ya-challenge">2019-ya-challenge</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2565618289" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14426379998972715506"><b>3.5 stars!</b><br/><br/><a href='https://s1279.photobucket.com/user/Christyb23/media/Book%20Reviews%2011/51902528_10105167289557178_3824979727857221632_n_zpsptitfmfi.jpg.html' target='_blank' rel='nofollow noopener'>
  <img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1549978076i/27051799._SX540_.jpg' alt=' photo 51902528_10105167289557178_3824979727857221632_n_zpsptitfmfi.jpg' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/>
</a><br/><br/>Angie Thomas' debut novel 'The Hate You Give' blew me away. I hate to compare it to this, because they are totally different stories, but I couldn't help myself. For me, this was good, but not near as good as THUG. Angie Thomas is an amazing writer and there was lots I loved about this book, but there were also things that missed the mark a bit. <br/><br/>Bri is a teenager and an aspiring rapper. She wants to make it big not only because she is talented and wants to be famous etc, but becaus</span>
  <span id="freeText14426379998972715506" style="display:none"><b>3.5 stars!</b><br><br><a href="https://s1279.photobucket.com/user/Christyb23/media/Book%20Reviews%2011/51902528_10105167289557178_3824979727857221632_n_zpsptitfmfi.jpg.html" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1549978076i/27051799._SX540_.jpg" alt=" photo 51902528_10105167289557178_3824979727857221632_n_zpsptitfmfi.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br>Angie Thomas' debut novel 'The Hate You Give' blew me away. I hate to compare it to this, because they are totally different stories, but I couldn't help myself. For me, this was good, but not near as good as THUG. Angie Thomas is an amazing writer and there was lots I loved about this book, but there were also things that missed the mark a bit. <br><br>Bri is a teenager and an aspiring rapper. She wants to make it big not only because she is talented and wants to be famous etc, but because she wants to help support her family. Times are hard, and now that her mom lost her job they're even harder. Bri feels a lot of pressure. Most of it she puts on herself, but her life is far from easy. I could sympathize with Bri. Growing up in poverty is not easy and I understood why she made a lot of the choices she made. <br><br>While on the come up, Bri has a lot of hard choices to make. There are people that want to take advantage, to use her to get ahead themselves. She finds out really fast who she can trust and that people will see you the way you portray. This was a tough lesson for her to learn. <br><i>
  <blockquote>“There's only so much you can take being described as somebody you're not.”</blockquote>
</i><br>There were so many great moments in this book and characters I loved. Bri's mom was probably my favorite. Jay had been through so much and overcame so much. She was genuine and only wanted what was best for her kids. I also loved Bri's brother and friends. This is one of those books, like THUG, I could see on the big screen. <br><br>Overall, I did enjoy this one. There was no huge thing that was wrong with it, it just didn't hit me like THUG did. It was still a worthy read and I'm glad I read it. It had emotion, humor, and a good message. Also, the audio book was excellent. Bahni Turpin (the narrator) killed it. If you're going to read it, I would highly recommend listening!</span>

          </span>

<div id="review_2325145013" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2325145013" />
    <a title="Erin" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/17957823-erin"><img alt="Erin" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1597778686p2/17957823.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2325145013?book_show_action=true">Feb 24, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Erin" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Erin" href="/user/show/17957823-erin">Erin</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="ebook " href="/book/show/35068618-on-the-come-up">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/17957823-erin?shelf=books-i-own">books-i-own</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2325145013" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16090043585610420641">Damn, I loved this book! <i> The Hate U Give</i> was one of my favorite reads in 2017 and it looks like <i> On the Come Up</i> is going to make my 2019 list. Angie Thomas absolutely nails "voice" and "characterization " in her storytelling and in 16 year old Brianna, an aspiring rapper, she creates a protagonist that I was cheering for from page one. <br/><br/><b> That's what we call our goal, the come up. It's when we finally make it with this rap stuff. I'm talking get-out-of-the-Garden-and-have-enough-money-to-never-wo</b></span>
  <span id="freeText16090043585610420641" style="display:none">Damn, I loved this book! <i> The Hate U Give</i> was one of my favorite reads in 2017 and it looks like <i> On the Come Up</i> is going to make my 2019 list. Angie Thomas absolutely nails "voice" and "characterization " in her storytelling and in 16 year old Brianna, an aspiring rapper, she creates a protagonist that I was cheering for from page one. <br /><br /><b> That's what we call our goal, the come up. It's when we finally make it with this rap stuff. I'm talking get-out-of-the-Garden-and-have-enough-money-to-never-worry-again make it. </b><br /><br />This will most likely not be a shock to anyone but I don't know a lot about the hip hop industry and the only time I really listen to rap music is when one of my high school students plays it during basketball in the gymnasium. But Angie Thomas was a teenage rapper at one time and the way this story unfolds certainly makes me wonder how much of the story is her actual story. So many characters remind Brianna to be true to herself, but I liked how Thomas really flicks the microscope on the industry, its artists, and social media.<br /><br />Another clear winner for me is that there are so many types of relationships in this story. Brianna and her mother, Jayda. The tight sibling relationship between Brianna and her big brother, Trey. Probably one of my all time favorite characters was Brianna's Aunt Pooh( Katricia), a member of a local gang who has always been Brianna's chief cheerleader when it comes to her music. <br /><br />So many characters and even though Brianna is the main lead, as a readerI felt really get to know so much about each of them and a sense of their importance in Brianna's life. There are just so many incredible scenes of dialogue between Brianna and the other characters. Without spoiling too much, there is this incredible scene between Jayda and her sister Katricia that still gets me a bit misty eyed.<br /><br />Like <i> The Hate U Give</i> Thomas also looks at racism in our society. Brianna's rap aspirations come head to head as she is dealing with something that happens at her school and in her home. When her fellow students use one of her songs in their peaceful protest, Brianna finds her identity struggles to now be interwoven with the music she writes. <br /><br /> But I don't want people thinking that this book is just heavy because there is plenty of laughter to be found too. Especially between Brianna and her pals Malik and Sonny.<br /><br /><i> Tweety Bird? The love of my life. Big Bird? I don't trust that ho. Plus, have you seen his nest? He probably hides bodies in it.</i> <br /><br /><i> But I guess Curtis is cute in the same way rodents are weirdly adorable. You know how you'll see a baby mouse and will be like "Aw, cute! Until that bitch is raiding your cabinet, eating the Halloween candy you hid from your little sisters. </i> <br /><br /><br />So I definitely loved this book. I certainly would recommend it to others. Even if you weren't a fan of The Hate U Give, give it a shot. Lastly, I would love to hear what other readers have thought and would appreciate a good discussion.</span>
  <a data-text-id="16090043585610420641" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2473843169" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2473843169" />
    <a title="Brandice" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/36348070-brandice"><img alt="Brandice" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1582594594p2/36348070.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2473843169?book_show_action=true">Nov 30, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Brandice" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Brandice" href="/user/show/36348070-brandice">Brandice</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/36578443-on-the-come-up">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2473843169" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5817622890438395167">Uh oh. After loving <i>The Hate U Give</i>, I was very excited to read Angie Thomas’s next book, <i>On the Come Up</i>. I’m bummed, however, to say it was just an ok read for me. <br/><br/>Sixteen-year old Bri Jackson lives in the Gardens but attends a prep school in another, better neighborhood. Her mom is 8 years clean, following the death of Bri’s dad, and is now going back to school to become a social worker. Her brother, Trey, recently graduated college and is living at home trying to help his family out - Bills a</span>
  <span id="freeText5817622890438395167" style="display:none">Uh oh. After loving <i>The Hate U Give</i>, I was very excited to read Angie Thomas’s next book, <i>On the Come Up</i>. I’m bummed, however, to say it was just an ok read for me. <br /><br />Sixteen-year old Bri Jackson lives in the Gardens but attends a prep school in another, better neighborhood. Her mom is 8 years clean, following the death of Bri’s dad, and is now going back to school to become a social worker. Her brother, Trey, recently graduated college and is living at home trying to help his family out - Bills and unsteady jobs threaten their stability. Her father, a local rapper, Lawless, died years ago. Bri also wants to be a rapper, often dubbed as “Lil Law” by others, but has difficultly breaking out of the shadow of her father, who was well-known in their neighborhood. <br /><br />Recognizing first and foremost this is a YA book and therefore I’m <i>not</i> the intended primary target audience, I have to say it <i>felt</i> very YA. The dialogue often seemed cheesy. For a book that was not the same as <i>T.H.U.G</i>, there appeared to be numerous similarities: a bad neighborhood (the same one in fact), an older brother the MC seems to idolize, and a stance against social injustice, though more subtle in <i>On the Come Up</i>. The ending also felt abrupt, possibly leaving the door open for future installments? <br /><br />This wasn’t a bad book and it has many great reviews - It just wasn’t for me. Maybe my expectations were too high after <i>T.H.U.G</i>, but I wasn’t wowed by <i>On the Come Up</i>.</span>
  <a data-text-id="5817622890438395167" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_2189853674" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2189853674" />
    <a title="mindful.librarian ☀️" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/13650342-mindful-librarian"><img alt="mindful.librarian ☀️" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1581440560p2/13650342.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2189853674?book_show_action=true">Feb 07, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="mindful.librarian ☀️" class="user" itemprop="url" name="mindful.librarian ☀️" href="/user/show/13650342-mindful-librarian">mindful.librarian ☀️</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="ebook " href="/book/show/35068618-on-the-come-up">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/13650342-mindful-librarian?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/13650342-mindful-librarian?shelf=aoc">aoc</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2189853674" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8126784666554795666">Angie Thomas didn't just live up to the expectations I had after reading and loving <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/32075671.The_Hate_U_Give' title='The Hate U Give by Angie Thomas' rel='nofollow noopener'>The Hate U Give</a>, she went to an entirely new level with On The Come Up. As a school librarian and reviewer of a great deal of young adult literature, I can tend to feel a bit of ”been there, read that" with many stories. This isn't a knock on YA, it's simply a result of being an adult reading a lot of YA. However, with On the Come Up, Angie Thomas brings a fresh and vital story to the genre, and also one of the m</span>
  <span id="freeText8126784666554795666" style="display:none">Angie Thomas didn't just live up to the expectations I had after reading and loving <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/32075671.The_Hate_U_Give" title="The Hate U Give by Angie Thomas" rel="nofollow noopener">The Hate U Give</a>, she went to an entirely new level with On The Come Up. As a school librarian and reviewer of a great deal of young adult literature, I can tend to feel a bit of ”been there, read that" with many stories. This isn't a knock on YA, it's simply a result of being an adult reading a lot of YA. However, with On the Come Up, Angie Thomas brings a fresh and vital story to the genre, and also one of the most amazing voices I have ever read in any level of literature.<br /><br />This story is about the systemic racism (and poverty) that prevails in America and the realities of so many Black youths in our country. It hits rap culture, racism, police brutality, gangs, drugs, and more. Thomas doesn't hold back in her scathing criticism of the current state of things (and many of the people) in fictional Garden Heights and the surrounding wealthier neighborhoods, projecting to the cities of the US as a whole. What impresses me the most is her ability to build empathy in readers for characters who so often are written as villains - she digs deep into why drug dealers are dealing, why addicts are using, why parents abandon their children, why families are living in poverty, why gang members are in gangs, why some rappers are using the lyrics that they do, and more. The why is honestly the most important part of all of those issues when reading through a critical lens with the knowledge of the systemic racism that has always plagued the US.<br /><br />Reading this book at the same time as <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/8171378.The_Warmth_of_Other_Suns_The_Epic_Story_of_America_s_Great_Migration" title="The Warmth of Other Suns The Epic Story of America's Great Migration by Isabel Wilkerson" rel="nofollow noopener">The Warmth of Other Suns: The Epic Story of America's Great Migration</a> and immediately following <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/29430746.Heavy_An_American_Memoir" title="Heavy An American Memoir by Kiese Laymon" rel="nofollow noopener">Heavy: An American Memoir</a> gave me such important context to bring to the story. I also recently read <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/38532160.Rap_Dad_A_Story_of_Family_and_the_Subculture_That_Shaped_a_Generation" title="Rap Dad A Story of Family and the Subculture That Shaped a Generation by Juan Vidal" rel="nofollow noopener">Rap Dad: A Story of Family and the Subculture That Shaped a Generation</a> which helped me immensely as a reader who listens to NO rap music, but holds a very healthy respect for the genre as a cultural standard.<br /><br />On the subject of issue book vs. non-issue book - this is a capital-I-issue book. And it's the gold standard of such. If you get a chance to listen to Angie Thomas' interview on the podcast "It's Been a Minute", please do. It added such a rich layer to my reading of this book because it made me understand completely who this book is for and the motivation for writing it. Thomas makes it blatantly clear this book is for the Black kids in neighborhoods like the one she grew up in in Jackson, Mississippi and how closely the neighborhood of Garden Heights is based on this same neighborhood. Sure, this book is a window for suburban white kids and middle-aged white women like me, but that's not who she's really doing the work for.<br /><br />In addition, her words in the interview about the attempts to ban The Hate U Give are spot on. When she describes how an 8-year-old wrote to her after reading it and said his mom gave it to him and he loved it, she talks about how some white moms are worried about their 13-year-olds reading it. She lays it out that if a Black mom feels that her young son needs this story because of his reality, then white moms shielding their teens from even reading about it is absolute privilege. That hit me so hard. The attempts to keep OTCU out of hands of teens will surely come, and I guarantee Bri would have words to throw back about it. This is the life and circumstances that teens are living, and the very least white parents and teachers/librarians can do is encourage more privileged kids to read it, rather than shield them from it. As for the kids that Thomas is writing for, let's all do our part to get this book to them. In any way possible.<br /><br />If you are a white adult who claims to "not read YA because I'm an adult", I challenge you to READ THIS BOOK. Open your mind. Listen. Learn. You don't need to review it, but know that Thomas is speaking her truth, as well as the truth of a vast number of people in our country. Honor them and hear the story.</span>
  <a data-text-id="8126784666554795666" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_3403616743" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/3403616743" />
    <a title="Carmen" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/25353295-carmen"><img alt="Carmen" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1412617445p2/25353295.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/3403616743?book_show_action=true">Jun 22, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Carmen" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Carmen" href="/user/show/25353295-carmen">Carmen</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="ebook " href="/book/show/35068618-on-the-come-up">review of another edition</a>

          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">Anyone</span></div>

        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/25353295-carmen?shelf=american-author">american-author</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/25353295-carmen?shelf=ya">ya</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/25353295-carmen?shelf=fiction">fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/25353295-carmen?shelf=published2019">published2019</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/25353295-carmen?shelf=traditionally-published">traditionally-published</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/25353295-carmen?shelf=she-says">she-says</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3403616743" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8490797225646169417"><i>It's like having a bucket of ice water thrown in my face.<br/><br/>Ratchet hood rat.<br/><br/>Thousands of people just heard me act like that. Millions more may see the video. They won't care that my life is a mess and I had every right to be mad. They'll just see an angry black girl from the ghetto, acting like they expected me to act.<br/><br/>Supreme laughs to himself. "You played the role," he says. "Goddamn, you played the role."<br/><br/>Problem is, I wasn't playing. That's what I've become.</i> pg. 355<br/><br/>OKAY, even though I was resist</span>
  <span id="freeText8490797225646169417" style="display:none"><i>It's like having a bucket of ice water thrown in my face.<br /><br />Ratchet hood rat.<br /><br />Thousands of people just heard me act like that. Millions more may see the video. They won't care that my life is a mess and I had every right to be mad. They'll just see an angry black girl from the ghetto, acting like they expected me to act.<br /><br />Supreme laughs to himself. "You played the role," he says. "Goddamn, you played the role."<br /><br />Problem is, I wasn't playing. That's what I've become.</i> pg. 355<br /><br />OKAY, even though I was resisting (RESISTING), I am going to have to give Angie Thomas five stars for this one.<br /><br /><b>Why were you resisting, Carmen?</b><br /><br />Well, you know. YA isn't my thing. I have an aversion to YA. Real-life teenagers? I like them. Fictional books about teenagers? Nah. They are usually forced, awkward, and lame. Just can't stand 90% of YA. It's so contrived. Probably because it's written by adults about alleged "teenaged" experiences.<br /><br />Secondly, the girl in here is a rapper trying to make it big. Music is not my thing, reading about music is definitely not my thing. I've said this before: play guitar? Think that's sexy? Not to me. Want to write a book about being a singer? Not for me. Playing piano and auditioning? No. So this rapping, make-it-big story is not my cup of tea. I don't give a shit. Any musical plot or plot that revolves around instruments or performing, singing, rapping, or being a musician is totally not interesting to me.<br /><br />Despite these two strikes against Thomas at the onset, she still managed to impress me a lot. She's a talented writer. She draws you into her story. She does a good job of blending the serious topics of her work (racism, gangs, protest/riots, poverty, drug addiction) which are very topical and more typical teenage dramas like is-he-going-to-kiss me?, will-my-mom-find-out?, and teenage friendships and their ups and downs.<br /><br />This could easily be very contrived. It could easily be awkward and lame. But Thomas is smooth. She is able to naturally blend everything together and do so with an authentic voice that doesn't make it seem like she is creating a narrative to fit her agenda. Instead, it seems like an honest-to-Betsy story with an honest-to-Betsy plot and real characters. Sure, it's YA, and therefore centers on teen issues (which might make some people weary) - Heaven knows 'teenage issues' make me weary - but for a YA book it's pretty natural and gripping.<br /><br />Same with the discussions of race and racial issues. Yes, it's very appropriate right now. But it's easy to jump on a topical current-events wagon and ride it for money. That's NOT what Thomas is doing here. When I first heard about <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/32075671.The_Hate_U_Give__The_Hate_U_Give___1_" title="The Hate U Give (The Hate U Give, #1) by Angie Thomas" rel="nofollow noopener">The Hate U Give</a>, that's what I thought Thomas was doing. Jumping on a current-events wagon, and with a fucking YA book to boot. However, I was wrong. I ended up giving <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/32075671.The_Hate_U_Give__The_Hate_U_Give___1_" title="The Hate U Give (The Hate U Give, #1) by Angie Thomas" rel="nofollow noopener">The Hate U Give</a> five stars. And now I've ended up giving this book five stars. That means something. Thomas can actually write.<br /><br />Yes, Bri, the main character in this book can be stupid at times. But she's a teenager. Teenagers do stupid things sometimes and don't think things through. (Ha ha, so do adults, but usually life has knocked some sense into them by then.) I usually am rolling my eyes, but I found Bri's moments of stupidity to be believable, even if I didn't enjoy them.<br /><br />Also, Bri stands up for herself brilliantly. Sure, there are some times in the book when she SHOULD stand up for herself and doesn't - but again, teenager. It's easier to railroad teenagers sometimes. But overall her self-confidence and ability to speak out was admirable and encouraging. I was cheering. She did not have the self-doubt I would have had in those situations. She tells off people with a clear voice, and I admire that. Her friends, her elders. She has a lot of courage. I admired that and respected it.<br /><br />It always seems like Thomas is writing a long-ass book - I'm always surprised by the length of her novels when I pick them up - but it goes quickly and I don't think she is padding it nor do I think she needed a better editor. The length suited the book. I feel like she needed the page-count in order to say what she needed to say. <br /><br />Another strike against Thomas is that this is her second book. The shininess has rubbed off. People know her schtick now. This can be awful - see <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/6540057.Andy_Weir" title="Andy Weir" rel="nofollow noopener">Andy Weir</a> or <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/31712.Ernest_Cline" title="Ernest Cline" rel="nofollow noopener">Ernest Cline</a> for examples of authors who blew people away with their first book only to sadly reveal that they were a one-trick pony with their second novel.<br /><br />I was afraid that was going to be Thomas, as well.<br /><br />Because, let's face it, she's writing about the same area, the same basic ideas, the same types of situations... it could have been a disaster.<br /><br />But it wasn't. Here's to hoping she's got a decent third novel inside of her.<br /><br /><br /><b>TL;DR</b> If you have hesitated to pick up an Angie Thomas book, I'd encourage you to give it a shot. I know it's tempting to dismiss her books as riding a current-events bandwagon, and the idea of suffering through a YA novel might make some people cringe. However, if you give her a shot you might be surprised. I certainly was. Her books are actually good, not your typical YA dreck and I feel like she writes flowing, authentic, naturally-formed stories instead of relying on trying to force some emotions and dialogue. Not an easy thing to do. Props to her. I'd recommend giving her a chance to impress you. If this cynical, hard-hearted reader actually enjoyed her books, there's hope. Not to mention I'm a YA-averse grump.<br /><br />If you care about representation, there are both gay male characters and lesbians in this book.<br /><br /><b>SOUNDTRACK FOR THE BOOK</b><br />“Flash Light” by Parliament <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=6F7xbF7OnxU">https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=6F7xb...</a><br /><br />“Sky's the Limit” by The Notorious B.I.G. <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=d3vOeCkeCNA">https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=d3vOe...</a><br /><br />“Kick in the Door” by The Notorious B.I.G. <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=ZRfnWpV4i7E">https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=ZRfnW...</a><br /><br />“A Tale of Two Citiez” by J. Cole <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=PB7gyS1TsYo">https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=PB7gy...</a><br /><br />“Niggas in Paris” by Jay-Z and Kanye <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=gG_dA32oH44&amp;list=PL914031C309E2285F&amp;index=181">https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=gG_dA...</a><br /><br />“Deep Cover” by Dr. Dre feat. Snoop Dogg <br /><a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=Op9Ml7pS6uA">https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=Op9Ml...</a><br /><br />“Shook Ones, Pt. II” by Mobb Deep <br /><a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=yoYZf-lBF_U">https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=yoYZf...</a><br /><br />“Silent Night” by The Temptations <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=D0mgk0KgI0Q">https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=D0mgk...</a><br /><br />“Fuck Tha Police” by NWA <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="https://youtu.be/Z7-TTWgiYL4">https://youtu.be/Z7-TTWgiYL4</a><br /><br />“P.Y.T.” by Michael Jackson <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=1ZZQuj6htF4">https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=1ZZQu...</a><br /><br />“Apparently” by J. Cole <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=eRaFMlZ1YHA">https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=eRaFM...</a><br /><br /><b>NAMES IN THIS BOOK</b><br /><a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[<br />Aunt Pooh f Katricia <br />Jay f Jayda <br />Brianna nn Bri f Breezy Bookie <br />Sonny m Jackson gay Jackson Emmanuel <br />Malik m<br />Lawless m<br />Trey m Lawrence Marshall <br />Long m<br />Tate m<br />Norma f<br />Lena f<br />Frank m<br />Reggie m<br />Dee-Nice m<br />DJ Hype m<br />M-Dot m<br />Ms. Tique f Kayla <br />CZ m<br />Milez m Miles <br />Supreme m Clarence <br />Shana f<br />Deon m<br />Zane m<br />Aja f<br />Keyona f<br />Nevaeh f<br />Jabari m<br />Curtis m<br />Keandre m<br />Aunt 'Chelle f<br />Jojo m<br />Scrap m<br />Tony m<br />Mr. Daryl m<br />Ms. Pat f<br />Ms. Sonja f<br />Gina f<br />Doc m<br />Louise f<br />Carol f<br />Big Sal f<br />Edward m<br />Ef-X m<br />Emily f<br />2Paw – cat <br />Kennedy f<br />Paris f<br />Skye f<br />Geraldine f<br />David m<br />Karen f<br />James m<br />Liz f<br /> <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span></span>

<div id="review_2683564550" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2683564550" />
    <a title="Jasmine from How Useful It Is" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4467515-jasmine-from-how-useful-it-is"><img alt="Jasmine from How Useful It Is" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1516737798p2/4467515.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2683564550?book_show_action=true">Mar 27, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Jasmine from How Useful It Is" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Jasmine from How Useful It Is" href="/user/show/4467515-jasmine-from-how-useful-it-is">Jasmine from How Useful It Is</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4467515-jasmine-from-how-useful-it-is?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4467515-jasmine-from-how-useful-it-is?shelf=library">library</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4467515-jasmine-from-how-useful-it-is?shelf=contemporary">contemporary</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2683564550" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17697961735507371084">I started reading On the Come Up on 3/16/2019 and finished it on 3/28/2019 at 12:30am. This book is an excellent read! I love that it takes place in the same neighborhood as the author’s first book and the bits and pieces of the first book were mentioned on here. I can’t recall if Bri’s dad was mentioned in The Hate U Give since I read it awhile ago. The characters are likeable. I like Bri’s older brother, Trey. He’s such a caring brother and a good son. I like Bri’s friends Sonny and Malik, esp</span>
  <span id="freeText17697961735507371084" style="display:none">I started reading On the Come Up on 3/16/2019 and finished it on 3/28/2019 at 12:30am. This book is an excellent read! I love that it takes place in the same neighborhood as the author’s first book and the bits and pieces of the first book were mentioned on here. I can’t recall if Bri’s dad was mentioned in The Hate U Give since I read it awhile ago. The characters are likeable. I like Bri’s older brother, Trey. He’s such a caring brother and a good son. I like Bri’s friends Sonny and Malik, especially Sonny and his out of this world specific examples and cute love life. I like Bri’s mom, more on how she protects her kids. I’m disappointed in her when she retreats into her room like a turtle hiding inside its shell. Despite their hardship, Bri’s mom wants no free handouts from her in-laws and wants her daughter to experience her teen life without worrying about bills. I like learning little life lessons from reading books and books by this author definitely has them.<br /><br />This book is told in the first person point of view following Brianna (Bri) Jackson, 16 as she attends an ACT prep class with her best buddies Malik and Sonny. Bri isn’t worry about the ACT, instead she’s waiting for a phone call. She wants to take part in the Ring, a place to give wannabe rappers a chance to be heard through a battle. Bri’s father was a rapper, known as the underground King until he was killed and Bri’s mother is a recovering drug addict. Bri’s older brother Trey, 22 graduated with honors but have a hard time finding a job. Their home life is hard especially when Bri’s mom loses her job. All Bri wants is to make it big as a rapper to improve her family’s life, but with what little she has to rely on, there will for sure be challenges. This book is divided into 3 parts.<br /><br />On the Come Up is very well written and hard to put down. I enjoy reading this book almost as much as the author’s debut, though, her debut makes me laugh more. That competitiveness between Bri’s family on the UNO game and Michael Jackson Wii game is fun to read. I like the bit of romance and flirting though I thought Bri shouldn’t let his hands wander on their first kiss. I like when books are written in the first person point of view because it feels realistic. I like learning how Bri experience discrimination and racism being an African American, either going to a store or attending a school that has fewer students of the same race. It reminds me of why I often stay away from entering those stores with few customers because I don’t enjoy the sales associates’ eyes on my back either. Another winner from Angie Thomas and I highly recommend everyone to read this book!<br /><br />Pro: fast paced, page turner, couldn’t put down, rap music, poetry, family, friendship, diversity, humor<br /><br />Con: none<br /><br />I rate it 5 stars!<br /><br />***Disclaimer: I borrowed this book from my local library and my opinions are honest.<br /><br />xoxo,<br /> Jasmine at <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="http://www.howusefulitis.wordpress.com">www.howusefulitis.wordpress.com</a> for more details</span>
  <a data-text-id="17697961735507371084" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/3460414590" />
    <a title="Lauren Lanz" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/82987361-lauren-lanz"><img alt="Lauren Lanz" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1586150400p2/82987361.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/3460414590?book_show_action=true">Jul 27, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Lauren Lanz" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Lauren Lanz" href="/user/show/82987361-lauren-lanz">Lauren Lanz</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/82987361-lauren-lanz?shelf=poc-rep">poc-rep</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/82987361-lauren-lanz?shelf=4-stars">4-stars</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/82987361-lauren-lanz?shelf=lgbtqia-rep">lgbtqia-rep</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/82987361-lauren-lanz?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/82987361-lauren-lanz?shelf=author-of-colour">author-of-colour</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/82987361-lauren-lanz?shelf=contemporary">contemporary</a>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3460414590" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2793053015568679462">This was a fantastic story, as to be expected from the author of <i>The Hate U Give</i>.<br/><br/><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i>“There's only so much you can take being described as somebody you're not.”</i>
  </b>
</blockquote><br/><br/><i>On the Come Up</i> follows Brianna Jackson, a sixteen year old aspiring rapper. With her mom struggling to pay rent and her school’s security guards targeting black and latinx students, Bri hopes that her raps are enough to warrant permanent change.<br/><br/>After a spectacular debut novel, I had high hopes for Angie Thomas and anything she wou</span>
  <span id="freeText2793053015568679462" style="display:none">This was a fantastic story, as to be expected from the author of <i>The Hate U Give</i>.<br /><br /><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i>“There's only so much you can take being described as somebody you're not.”</i>
  </b>
</blockquote><br /><br /><i>On the Come Up</i> follows Brianna Jackson, a sixteen year old aspiring rapper. With her mom struggling to pay rent and her school’s security guards targeting black and latinx students, Bri hopes that her raps are enough to warrant permanent change.<br /><br />After a spectacular debut novel, I had high hopes for Angie Thomas and anything she would put a pen to in the future. Those hopes were not misplaced, as this book certainly delivered a powerful punch.<br /><br />Bri is a protagonist that grasped my interest from the start. It was so gripping to follow her through rap battles and ongoing personal struggles. Thomas manages to capture and narrate several important topics through Bri, topics like poverty, racism, violence and addiction. I could hardly stop reading because of how strong the narrative was.<br /><br />It was really interesting to see Bri navigate the world of hip hop at such a young age. The author does a nice job demonstrating the protagonist’s youth through bad decisions and strong will. Bri’s friends and family were all well developed and frequently present in the story, too, which I loved to see.<br /><br />I can hardly complain about what was delivered. This is a great story.</span>
  <a data-text-id="2793053015568679462" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Audiobook 9781509475506" href="/book/show/39829113-on-the-come-up">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/16254355-matthew?shelf=2020">2020</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/16254355-matthew?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>,

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3141545021" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7159865104921281037">Sometimes you just like a book or an author that is not something you would normally like. Or, maybe it is a topic or genre that others might think don't match your demographic. So far I have read two Angie Thomas books and loved them even though the target demographic is definitely not me! She writes so well and I get very into the story and characters. I have to say that for me she is one of the most impressive contemporary authors.<br/><br/>I listened to this book and I have to give props to Bahni Turp</span>
  <span id="freeText7159865104921281037" style="display:none">Sometimes you just like a book or an author that is not something you would normally like. Or, maybe it is a topic or genre that others might think don't match your demographic. So far I have read two Angie Thomas books and loved them even though the target demographic is definitely not me! She writes so well and I get very into the story and characters. I have to say that for me she is one of the most impressive contemporary authors.<br><br>I listened to this book and I have to give props to Bahni Turpin. She is a fantastic audiobook narrator. She does all the different voices, male and female, perfectly. I think my experience with this book was enhanced because I got a chance to listen to her. If you have not taken the opportunity to do a Bahni Turpin audiobook, you really should give it a try.<br><br>Again, this book may not be written for your demographic, but the way it is written in transcends all the demographic lines. Give it a shot, it is so well done I think you will thank me for recommending it! <br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1595302405i/29847755.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"></span>

//<![CDATA[  

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('HboqBSnzqDBnRGY60jor+38erlSdr5ojRmKQH/dvBVbWWptuMqxs95AWjGlcDzib9oi1pfJOcdzJcRrbGNLWew==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('jOtQdmIpiCh7tPRgAZj7NL+ILl0O6o/ih6bPGYlPT4FHC+EdeXZM74zmHjOPrehUNh41rGELZB0ItUXdZvKcrA==')})
  }
//]]>
</script>

<span id="freeTextContainer13656705986428306044">Angie Thomas was born, raised, and still resides in Jackson, Mississippi as indicated by her accent. She is a former teen rapper whose greatest accomplishment was an article about her in Right-On Magazine with a picture included. She holds a BFA in Creative Writing from Belhaven University and an unofficial degree in Hip Hop. She can also still rap if needed. She is an inaugural winner of the Walt</span>
  <span id="freeText13656705986428306044" style="display:none">Angie Thomas was born, raised, and still resides in Jackson, Mississippi as indicated by her accent. She is a former teen rapper whose greatest accomplishment was an article about her in Right-On Magazine with a picture included. She holds a BFA in Creative Writing from Belhaven University and an unofficial degree in Hip Hop. She can also still rap if needed. She is an inaugural winner of the Walter Dean Meyers Grant 2015, awarded by We Need Diverse Books. Her debut novel, The Hate U Give, was acquired by Balzer + Bray/HarperCollins in a 13-house auction and will be published in spring 2017. Film rights have been optioned by Fox 2000 with George Tillman attached to direct and Hunger Games actress Amandla Stenberg set to star.</span>
  <a data-text-id="13656705986428306044" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>
